Buyu — Sales and Trade
beginner
8 min
Ruling: Simultaneous Delivery in Barter
Rules that in barter or exchange of prices, both deliver at once

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that delivery must be simultaneous in barter and exchanges of prices, and identify the proofs (companion practice and hadith) that support it.

Core Idea
In barter and currency exchange, both parties must deliver at the same time — simultaneous delivery is wajib.

This passage from Al-Quduri deals with a fundamental principle in sales: when goods are swapped for goods, or when one price (currency) is exchanged for another, the transaction must be executed immediately by both sides. You will see how the Hanafi school uses both a companion practice (Ibn Umar) and a prophetic hadith to derive the obligation of simultaneous delivery.

Guided Path
1
Understand the transaction type
Identify that the ruling covers two cases: selling goods for goods (barter) and selling a price for a price (currency exchange).
Price (thaman) here refers to dirhams and dinars or any medium of exchange.
2
Note the obligation
The text says 'قِيلَ لَهُمَا سَلِّمَا مَعًا' — it is said to them both: 'Deliver simultaneously.' This is a wajib obligation.
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub).
3
Examine the first proof
The practice of Ibn Umar (companion) and the fatwa of Sa'id ibn Jubayr allows taking dirhams from dinars and vice versa without specifying the exact coins, implying immediate exchange.
This demonstrates that the exchange is valid only when done hand-to-hand.
4
Examine the second proof
The hadith of Ubadah ibn al-Samit from the Prophet (peace be upon him) commands: 'Sell gold for silver however you wish hand to hand' (يدًا بيد). This establishes simultaneous delivery for like-kind exchanges.
The hadith is from Sunan al-Tirmidhi (no. 1240), classified as ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is wajib not fard.
5
Recognize the usul principles
The passage concludes with two principles: (1) The price (thaman) is not determined merely by specification; actual delivery fixes it. (2) If the goods and price are from the same category, simultaneous delivery is mandatory to avoid riba.
These principles reinforce the need for immediate exchange.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ بَاعَ سِلْعَةً بِسِلْعَةٍ أَوْ ثُمَنًا بِثَمَنٍ قِيلَ لَهُمَا سَلِّمَا مَعًا وَجْهٌ : (۱) قَوْلُ الصَّحَابِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ بَاعَ سِلْعَةً بِسِلْعَةٍ أَوْ ثُمَنًا بِثَمَنٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ أَنَّهُ كَانَ لَا يَرَى بَأْسًا أَنْ يَأْخُذَ الدَّرَاهِمَ مِنَ الدَّنَانِيرِ، وَالدَّنَانِيرَ مِنَ الدَّرَاهِمِ قَالَ دَاوُدُ: وَكَانَ سَعِيدُ بْنُ جُبَيْرٍ يُفْتِي بِهِ (مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، بَابُ : الرَّجُلُ عَلَيْهِ فِضَّةٌ أَيَأْخُذُ مَكَانَهُ ذَهَبًا، نُمْبِر ١٤٥٧٧) وَجْهٌ (۲) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنْ بَاعَ سِلْعَةً بِسِلْعَةٍ أَوْ ثُمَنًا بِثَمَنٍ عَنْ عُبَادَةَ بْنِ الصَّامِتِ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الذَّهَبُ بِالذَّهَبِ مِثْلًا بِمِثْلٍ، بِيعُوا الذَّهَبَ بِالْفِضَّةِ كَيْفَ شِئْتُمْ يَدًا بِيَدٍ، وَبِيعُوا الْبُرَّ بِالتَّمْرِ كَيْفَ شِئْتُمْ يَدًا بِيَدٍ» (سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ أَنَّ الْحِنْطَةَ بِالْحِنْطَةِ مِثْلٌ بِمِثْلٍ وَكَرَاهِيَةُ التَّفَاضُلِ فِيهِ، نُمْبِر ١٢٤٠) أُصُولٌ : ثَمَنٌ دِرْهَمٌ وَدَنَانِيرُ مُتَعَيِّنٌ مِنْ غَيْرِ مُتَعَيِّنٍ لَا يَتَعَيَّنُ، الْبَتَّةَ سَامَانٌ مُتَعَيِّنٌ يَصِيرُ. أُصُولٌ : مُبِيعٌ وَثَمَنٌ إِذَا كَانَ مِنْ قَبِيلٍ وَاحِدٍ فَإِنَّ الْبَائِعَ وَالْمُشْتَرِيَ كِلَيْهِمَا يَأْخُذَانِ وَيُعْطِيَانِ مَعًا.
And whoever sells goods for goods, or a price for a price, it is said to them both: 'Deliver simultaneously.' Proof (1): The saying of the companion for establishing that whoever sells goods for goods or a price for a price: from Ibn Umar that he saw no harm in taking dirhams from dinars and dinars from dirhams. Dawud said: Sa'id ibn Jubayr used to give a fatwa by it. (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq, no. 14577) Proof (2): The hadith for establishing that whoever sells goods for goods or a price for a price: from Ubadah ibn al-Samit, from the Prophet, he said: 'Gold for gold like for like, sell gold for silver however you wish hand to hand, and sell wheat for dates however you wish hand to hand.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, no. 1240) Principles: The price, dirhams and dinars, are not determined by specification, but the goods become determined. Another principle: If the goods and the price are from the same category, then the seller and buyer both take and give together.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This section covers barter and exchange of one price for another (e.g., currency exchange). In such transactions, both parties must deliver their items simultaneously. The first proof is the practice of Ibn Umar allowing exchange of silver for gold without specifying the exact coins, implying immediate exchange. The second proof is the hadith of Ubadah requiring hand-to-hand delivery in exchanges of like items. The two principles at the end clarify that in a sale, the price (thaman) is not fixed merely by specifying dirhams and dinars; actual delivery determines it. And if the goods and price belong to the same category (e.g., both are currency or both are food items of the same type), simultaneous delivery is required to avoid riba.

Key Terms
ثُمَنٌ (thuman): Price (plural of thaman); here it refers to currency or any medium of exchange.
يدًا بيد (yadan bi yad): Hand to hand; meaning immediate, simultaneous delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When goods are exchanged for goods (barter), how must delivery occur according to this passage?
A) Seller delivers first, then buyer
B) Buyer delivers first, then seller
C) Both deliver simultaneously
D) Delivery can be deferred

Key Takeaway
In barter and currency exchange, both parties must deliver simultaneously; deferral invalidates the sale.

Khiyar al-Shart: Duration and Ownership Disputes
Intra-Hanafi dispute on duration and ownership in khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the maximum duration of khiyar al-shart and the buyer's ownership during the option period, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreements.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa limits khiyar al-shart to three days and says buyer does not own; Sahibayn allow any known period and say buyer owns.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn addresses two key intra-Hanafi disputes in khiyar al-shart. First, how long may the option period last? Second, who bears the risk of loss during the buyer's option? Understanding these disagreements and their proofs is essential for correctly applying the rulings in sale contracts.

Guided Path
1
State the permissibility of khiyar al-shart
Identify the act: the option of condition is permissible in sales for both parties. This is the basic ruling.
2
Analyze the duration dispute
Abu Hanifa holds the maximum is three days or less; Sahibayn allow any specified known period. Identify the proof: the hadith 'The option is three days.'
The hadith is from Darqutni and Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the ownership dispute
During the buyer's option, Abu Hanifa says the buyer does not own the item (risk on seller); Sahibayn say he owns it (risk on buyer). Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: if the item perishes, who bears the loss?
According to Sahibayn, it perishes at the price; according to Abu Hanifa, the buyer is liable for market value.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view: three-day limit and buyer does not own during his option.
The matn presents Abu Hanifa's view as the default.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ جَائِزٌ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِلْبَائِعِ وَالْمُشْتَرِي وَلَهُمَا الْخَيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا وَلَا يَجُوزُ أَكْثَرُ مِنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ إِذَا سَمَّيَا مُدَّةً مَعْلُومَةً وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْكِهِ فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فِي مُدَّةِ الْخِيَارِ ضَمِنَهُ بِالْقِيمَةِ وَخِيَارُ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْكِ الْبَائِعِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُشْتَرِيَ لَا يَمْلِكُهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَمْلِكُهُ فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ هَلَكَ بِالثَّمَنِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ دَخَلَهُ عَيْبٌ وَمَنْ شُرِطَ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَفْسَخَ فِي مُدَّةِ الْخِيَارِ وَلَهُ أَنْ يُجِيزَهُ وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ بِالْخِيَارِ فِي بَيْعِهِمَا مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا أَوْ يَكُونَ الْبَيْعُ خِيَارًا» (صحيح البخاري، نُمْبِر ٢١٠٧ / صحيح مسلم، نُمْبِر ١٥٣١ / سُنَنُ أَبِي دَاوُدَ، نُمْبِر ٣٤٥٤) وَجْهٌ : (۱) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ» (سُنَنُ الدَّارَقُطْنِيِّ، نُمْبِر ٣٠١٢ / سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، نُمْبِر ١٢٥٢) وَجْهٌ : (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْكِهِ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَا يَتَفَرَّقَنَّ عَنْ بَيْعٍ إِلَّا عَنْ تَرَاضٍ» (سُنَنُ التِّرْمِذِيِّ، نُمْبِر ١٢٤٨) وَجْهٌ : (۱) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فَقَالَ شُرَيْحٌ لِعُمَرَ: أَخَذْتَهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا وَأَنْتَ لَهُ ضَامِنٌ حَتَّى تَرُدَّهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا (السُّنَنُ الْكُبْرَى لِلْبَيْهَقِيِّ، نُمْبِر ١٠٤٦٣ / مُصَنَّفُ عَبْدِ الرَّزَّاقِ، نُمْبِر ١٤٩٧٨) أُصُولٌ : إِيجَابٌ وَقَبُولٌ ہونے کے بعد متعاقدین کو بیع کے نافذ کرنے یا رد کرنے کا اختیار ہونا جائز ہے۔ أُصُولٌ : بائع کی پوری رضامندی کے بغیر مبیع اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں نکلے گی۔
Chapter of Option of Condition. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - Option of condition is permissible in sale for the seller and the buyer, and they have the option for three days or less, and it is not permissible for more than that according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is permissible if they specify a known period. The seller's option prevents the goods from leaving his ownership; so if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand during the option period, he is liable for its value. And the buyer's option does not prevent the goods from leaving the seller's ownership by consensus, except that the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: He owns it. So if it perishes in his hand, it perishes at the price; similarly if a defect occurs. And whoever is given the option may cancel during the option period and may confirm it. Proof (1): The hadith for establishing the option of condition: from Ibn Umar from the Prophet: 'The two transactors have the option in their sale as long as they have not separated or the sale is an option sale.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) Proof (1) for establishing that they have the option for three days: from Ibn Umar from the Prophet: 'The option is three days.' (Darqutni, Tirmidhi) Proof (1) for establishing that the seller's option prevents the goods from leaving his ownership: from Abu Hurayra from the Prophet: 'Do not separate from a sale except with mutual consent.' (Tirmidhi) Proof (1): The saying of the tabi'i for establishing that if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand: Shurayh said to Umar: 'You took it sound and safe, and you are liable for it until you return it sound and safe.' (Baihaqi, Abd al-Razzaq) Principles: After offer and acceptance, it is permissible for the contractors to have the option to execute or cancel the sale. Another principle: The goods will not leave the seller's hand without his full consent.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This is the chapter on Khiyar al-Shart from Al-Quduri. It contains two intra-Hanafi disputes. First: the maximum duration. Abu Hanifa limits it to three days or less; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allow any agreed known period. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's three-day limit, as stated in the matn. Second: during the buyer's option period, whether the buyer owns the item. Abu Hanifa says the buyer does not own it (so risk remains with seller); Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say the buyer owns it (so risk on buyer). The proofs include the famous hadith 'The two transactors have the option...' which is the basis for khiyar. Another hadith fixes the option at three days, and the hadith 'Do not separate except with mutual consent' supports that the seller's option prevents final transfer. The saying of Shurayh to Umar establishes the buyer's liability when in possession. The two principles at the end summarize: the option is valid after offer and acceptance, and the seller's full consent is required for the goods to leave his ownership.

Key Terms
خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ (khiyār al-sharṭ): A stipulation in a sale contract allowing one or both parties to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period.
خِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ (khiyār al-bā'iʿ): An option stipulated for the seller, which prevents the goods from leaving the seller's ownership during the option period.
خِيَارُ الْمُشْتَرِي (khiyār al-mushtarī): An option stipulated for the buyer; it does not prevent the goods from leaving the seller's ownership but affects risk.
ثَمَرَةُ الْخِلَافِ (thamarah al-khilāf): The practical consequence of a legal disagreement; here, who bears the loss if the item perishes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens to the liability if the item perishes in the buyer's hand during the buyer's option period?
A) The buyer is liable for the market value.
B) The buyer is liable for the price.
C) The seller bears the loss because buyer does not own.
D) The buyer and seller split the loss.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa's view on khiyar al-shart limits the duration to three days and denies buyer ownership during his option, shaping liability rules in sales.

Duration of Khayar al-Shart: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Ruling on duration of khayar al-shart with intra-Hanafi dispute and hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the maximum duration of khayar al-shart and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn with reference to the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Option of stipulation is permissible up to three days per Abu Hanifa; Sahibayn allow any known period.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling on khayar al-shart (option of stipulation) from the matn of Al-Quduri. The passage establishes the permissibility of this option and immediately presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute: the maximum duration. We will analyze the proof used by each side and see how the practical ruling changes based on which view is followed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Khayar al-shart is ja'iz (permissible) in sales for both parties. This is the default ruling.
2
Locate the dispute
Abu Hanifa says maximum three days; Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say any known period (mudda ma'luma) is valid.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The hadith 'الخيار ثلاثة أيام' is cited. Abu Hanifa interprets this as a binding limit.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), but it is used as evidence for the restriction.
4
Analyze the Sahibayn's counter-proof
Sahibayn argue the hadith does not explicitly forbid more than three days; the key is that the period must be known (mudda ma'luma) to avoid uncertainty.
They prioritize the principle of preventing dispute (gharar) over the literal wording.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If parties stipulate a 10-day option, under Abu Hanifa the option is invalid and the sale is immediately binding; under Sahibayn the option is valid and the sale is suspended.
Later fatwa often follows Sahibayn for practicality.

Source Text

بَابُ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ جَائِزَ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِلْبَائِعِ وَالْمُشْتَرِي لَوَلَهُمَا الْخَيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْثَرُ مِنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ إِذَا سَمَّيَا مُدَّةً مَعْلُومَةً وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمَنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيع مِنْ مِلْكِهِ فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فِي مُدَّةِ الخيَارِ ضَمِنَهُ بِالْقِيمَةِ وَخِيَارُ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْك الْبَائِعِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْلِكُهُ عِندَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَمْلِكُهُ فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ هَلَكَ بِالثَّمَنِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ دَخَلَهُ عَيْبٌ وَمَنْ شُرِطَ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَفْسَخَ فِي مُدَّةِ الْخِيَارِ وَلَهُ أَنْ يُجِيزَهُ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِنَّ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ بِالْخِيَارِ فِي بَيْعِهِمَا مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا أَوْ يَكُونُ الْبَيْعُ خِيَارًا. »» (بخاري شريف بَابٌ كَمْ يَجُوزُ الْخِيَارُ ، نمبر 2107 / مسلم شريف: بَابٌ: كَمْ يَجُوزُ الْخِيَارُ،نمبر1531/(سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي خِيَارِ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ، نمبر 3454) ل وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ» (سنن دار قطني، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر3012 /سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي المُصَرَّاةِ، نمبر 1252) وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْكِهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَتَفَرَّقَنَّ عَنْ بَيْعِ إِلَّا عَنْ تَرَاضٍ» (سنن الترمذي، باب، نمبر 1248) وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ فَقَالَ شُرَيْحٌ لِعُمَرَ: أَخَذْتَهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا وَأَنْتَ لَهُ ضَامِنٌ حَتَّى تَرُدَّهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا ، " ( السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ الْمَأْخُوذِ عَلَى طَرِيقِ السَّوْمِ وَعَلَى بَيْعِ شُرِطَ فِيهِ الْخِيَارُ ، نمبر 10463/مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي الشَّيْءَ عَلَى أَنْ يُجَرِّبَهُ فَيَهْلَكَ، غمبر 14978) اصول : ایجاب و قبول ہونے کے بعد متعاقدین کو بیچ کے نافذ کرنے یارد کرنے کا اختیار ہونا جائز ہے۔
اصول : بائع کی پوری رضامندی کے بغیر مبیع اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں نکلے گی۔
فَإِنْ اخْتَارَ الْإِجَازَةَ بِغَيْرِ حَضْرَةِ صَاحِبِهِ جَازَ وَإِنْ فَسَخَ لَمْ يَجْزَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْآخَرُ حَاضِرًا ك وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ بَطَلَ خِيَارُهُ وَلَمْ يَنْتَقِلْ إِلَى وَرَثَتِهِ
وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ فَكَانَ بِخِلَافِ ذَلِكَ فَالْمُشْتَرِي بِالخَيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ جَمِيعِ الثَّمَنِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَهُ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ اخْتَارَ الْإِجَازَةَ بِغَيْرِ حَضْرَةِ صَاحِبِهِ جَازَ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ ، ، قَالَ: «لَا ضَرَرَ وَلَا ضِرَارَ» (سنن دار قطني فِي الْمَرْأَةِ تُقْتَلُ إِذَا ارْتَدَّتْ، نمبر 4539) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ بَطَلَ خِيَارُهُ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي اللَّهُ عنهما: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُتَبَايِعَانِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ عَلَى صَاحِبِهِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، إِلَّا بَيْعَ الخيار . » » (بخاري شريف بَابُ الْبَيْعَانِ بِالْخِيَارِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، نمبر 2111) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الغَرَرِ، وَبَيْعِ الحَصَاةِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْغَرَرِ، غير (1230) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازُ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما: «أَنَّ رَجُلًا ذَكَرَ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ يُخْدَعُ فِي الْبُيُوعِ، فَقَالَ: إِذَا بَايَعْتَ فَقُلْ لَا خِلَابَةَ».»» (بخاري شريف بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الْخِدَاعِ فِي الْبَيْعِ، نمبر 2117) ه اصول : بیج مکمل ہو جائے تو شمن لازم ہو جاتا ہے۔
اصول : مفت مرغوب فیہ کے فوت ہونے سے مشتری کو بیچ توڑنے کا اختیار ہو گا۔
Chapter of the Option of Stipulation. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - The option of stipulation is permissible in sale for the seller and the buyer, and both have the option for three days or less, and more than that is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is permissible if they specify a known period. The seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership; so if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand during the option period, he is liable for its value. The buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership by consensus, except that the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said he owns it. If it perishes in his hand, it perishes against the price, and likewise if a defect occurs in it. The one for whom the option is stipulated may cancel during the option period, and he may confirm it. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'both have the option for three days or less' from Ibn Umar, from the Prophet (PBUH) who said: 'The two parties in a sale have the option in their sale as long as they have not separated or the sale is an option sale.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). Also the hadith to establish 'both have the option for three days or less' from Ibn Umar: 'The option is three days' (Darqutni, Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'the seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership' from Abu Hurairah: 'Do not separate from a sale except by mutual consent' (Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish 'if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand' - Shurayh said to Umar: 'You took it sound and safe, and you are liable for it until you return it sound and safe' (Baihaqi, Abd al-Razzaq). Principles: After offer and acceptance, it is permissible for the contracting parties to have the option to execute or cancel the sale. Principle: The sold item will not leave the seller's hand without his full consent. Then if he chooses confirmation in the absence of the other party, it is valid; and if he cancels, it is not valid unless the other is present. And when the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. And whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe, and he is contrary to that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes he may take him for the full price, and if he wishes he may leave him. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'if he chooses confirmation in the absence of the other party, it is valid' from Aisha: 'There is no harm or reciprocating harm' (Darqutni). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'when the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void' from Ibn Umar: 'The two parties in a sale each have the option against the other as long as they have not separated, except for an option sale' (Bukhari). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe' from Abu Hurairah: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade the sale of uncertainty and the sale of pebbles' (Tirmidhi). Evidence: (2) The hadith to establish 'whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe' from Ibn Umar: 'A man mentioned to the Prophet (PBUH) that he was deceived in sales, so he said: When you make a sale, say: No deception' (Bukhari). Principles: When the sale is completed, the price becomes obligatory. Principle: With the death of the desired object, the buyer gets the option to cancel the sale.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the option of stipulation (khayar al-shart) in the Hanafi matn of Al-Quduri, accompanied by hadith proofs and usul principles. The author first states the ruling: it is permissible for either party to stipulate an option period in a sale, with a maximum of three days according to Imam Abu Hanifa. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that any specified period is valid as long as it is known. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text then explains the legal effect of the seller's option: the seller retains ownership during the option period, so if the buyer takes possession and the item is destroyed, the buyer is liable for its value. The reasoning is that the seller has not fully consented to transfer ownership. For the buyer's option, there is consensus that ownership transfers from the seller, but Abu Hanifa says the buyer does not actually own it until he confirms, while the two students say he does own it. Thus, if the item perishes in the buyer's hands, under Abu Hanifa the buyer is liable for the value (since he didn't own it), but under Sahibayn he is liable for the price (since he owned it). The party with the option may either confirm or cancel the sale within the stipulated period. The text then provides hadith evidence for each point, including the famous hadith 'The option is three days' and the principle that sales require consent. On page 308, the text continues: if the option-holder confirms the sale in the absence of the other party, it is valid; but cancellation requires the other's presence, because cancellation is a dissolution of contract which needs mutual agreement. The death of the option-holder voids his option and it does not pass to heirs, because the option is a personal right attached to the living individual. Finally, if someone sells a slave described as having a specific skill (baker or scribe) and the description is false, the buyer has the option to either take the slave for the full price or return it. This is based on the prohibition of deceit and uncertainty in sales. The usul principles at the end emphasize that after offer and acceptance, the parties have the right to execute or cancel, and that the sold item cannot leave the seller's hand without his full consent.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khayar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract allowing one or both parties to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period.
مدة معلومة (mudda ma'luma): A known and specified duration, without uncertainty, for the option period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, what is the maximum duration for an option of stipulation (khayar al-shart)?
A) One day
B) Three days
C) Seven days
D) Any specified period

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the option of stipulation, but the maximum duration is disputed: three days per Abu Hanifa, any known period per Sahibayn, with later fatwa often following the latter.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Ownership and Liability During the Option Period
Rulings on ownership and liability during seller's and buyer's option with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to differentiate the legal effects of seller's option and buyer's option on ownership and liability, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on the buyer's ownership during the option period.

Core Idea
During seller's option, buyer is liable for value; during buyer's option, liability is for the price per Sahibayn, value per Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines how khayar al-shart affects ownership and liability for loss or defect. The text distinguishes between seller's option and buyer's option, and again presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the buyer actually owns the item during his option period. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly assigning liability in case of destruction or defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Seller's option (khayar al-ba'i') and buyer's option (khayar al-mushtari).
2
Analyze seller's option effect
The seller retains ownership during the option period. If the buyer takes possession and the item perishes, the buyer is liable for its market value (qima).
Reason: ownership did not transfer, so the buyer is a trusted bailee but liable for negligence? Actually, he is liable for value because he has possession without ownership.
3
Analyze buyer's option effect
By consensus, the buyer's option does not prevent ownership from leaving the seller. Ownership transfers from the seller to the buyer immediately upon contracting, but the buyer's ownership is disputed.
Consensus: the item is no longer in the seller's ownership.
4
Understand the dispute on buyer's ownership
Abu Hanifa says the buyer does not own the item during the option period. Sahibayn say the buyer owns it.
This affects liability: if the item perishes, under Abu Hanifa the buyer must pay the value (qima); under Sahibayn the buyer pays the price (thaman).
5
Determine the liability consequence
If the item perishes in the buyer's hands: Abu Hanifa -> buyer pays value; Sahibayn -> buyer pays price. Also applies if a defect occurs.
The text states 'halka bi al-thaman' (perishes against the price) for the Sahibayn view.

بَابُ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ جَائِزَ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِلْبَائِعِ وَالْمُشْتَرِي لَوَلَهُمَا الْخَيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْثَرُ مِنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ إِذَا سَمَّيَا مُدَّةً مَعْلُومَةً وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمَنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيع مِنْ مِلْكِهِ فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فِي مُدَّةِ الخيَارِ ضَمِنَهُ بِالْقِيمَةِ وَخِيَارُ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْك الْبَائِعِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْلِكُهُ عِندَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَمْلِكُهُ فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ هَلَكَ بِالثَّمَنِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ دَخَلَهُ عَيْبٌ وَمَنْ شُرِطَ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَفْسَخَ فِي مُدَّةِ الْخِيَارِ وَلَهُ أَنْ يُجِيزَهُ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِنَّ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ بِالْخِيَارِ فِي بَيْعِهِمَا مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا أَوْ يَكُونُ الْبَيْعُ خِيَارًا. »» (بخاري شريف بَابٌ كَمْ يَجُوزُ الْخِيَارُ ، نمبر 2107 / مسلم شريف: بَابٌ: كَمْ يَجُوزُ الْخِيَارُ،نمبر1531/(سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي خِيَارِ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ، نمبر 3454) ل وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ» (سنن دار قطني، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر3012 /سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي المُصَرَّاةِ، نمبر 1252) وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْكِهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَتَفَرَّقَنَّ عَنْ بَيْعِ إِلَّا عَنْ تَرَاضٍ» (سنن الترمذي، باب، نمبر 1248) وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ فَقَالَ شُرَيْحٌ لِعُمَرَ: أَخَذْتَهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا وَأَنْتَ لَهُ ضَامِنٌ حَتَّى تَرُدَّهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا ، " ( السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ الْمَأْخُوذِ عَلَى طَرِيقِ السَّوْمِ وَعَلَى بَيْعِ شُرِطَ فِيهِ الْخِيَارُ ، نمبر 10463/مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي الشَّيْءَ عَلَى أَنْ يُجَرِّبَهُ فَيَهْلَكَ، غمبر 14978) اصول : ایجاب و قبول ہونے کے بعد متعاقدین کو بیچ کے نافذ کرنے یارد کرنے کا اختیار ہونا جائز ہے۔
اصول : بائع کی پوری رضامندی کے بغیر مبیع اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں نکلے گی۔
فَإِنْ اخْتَارَ الْإِجَازَةَ بِغَيْرِ حَضْرَةِ صَاحِبِهِ جَازَ وَإِنْ فَسَخَ لَمْ يَجْزَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْآخَرُ حَاضِرًا ك وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ بَطَلَ خِيَارُهُ وَلَمْ يَنْتَقِلْ إِلَى وَرَثَتِهِ
وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ فَكَانَ بِخِلَافِ ذَلِكَ فَالْمُشْتَرِي بِالخَيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ جَمِيعِ الثَّمَنِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَهُ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ اخْتَارَ الْإِجَازَةَ بِغَيْرِ حَضْرَةِ صَاحِبِهِ جَازَ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ ، ، قَالَ: «لَا ضَرَرَ وَلَا ضِرَارَ» (سنن دار قطني فِي الْمَرْأَةِ تُقْتَلُ إِذَا ارْتَدَّتْ، نمبر 4539) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ بَطَلَ خِيَارُهُ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي اللَّهُ عنهما: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُتَبَايِعَانِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ عَلَى صَاحِبِهِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، إِلَّا بَيْعَ الخيار . » » (بخاري شريف بَابُ الْبَيْعَانِ بِالْخِيَارِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، نمبر 2111) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الغَرَرِ، وَبَيْعِ الحَصَاةِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْغَرَرِ، غير (1230) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازُ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما: «أَنَّ رَجُلًا ذَكَرَ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ يُخْدَعُ فِي الْبُيُوعِ، فَقَالَ: إِذَا بَايَعْتَ فَقُلْ لَا خِلَابَةَ».»» (بخاري شريف بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الْخِدَاعِ فِي الْبَيْعِ، نمبر 2117) ه اصول : بیج مکمل ہو جائے تو شمن لازم ہو جاتا ہے۔
اصول : مفت مرغوب فیہ کے فوت ہونے سے مشتری کو بیچ توڑنے کا اختیار ہو گا۔
Chapter of the Option of Stipulation. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - The option of stipulation is permissible in sale for the seller and the buyer, and both have the option for three days or less, and more than that is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is permissible if they specify a known period. The seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership; so if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand during the option period, he is liable for its value. The buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership by consensus, except that the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said he owns it. If it perishes in his hand, it perishes against the price, and likewise if a defect occurs in it. The one for whom the option is stipulated may cancel during the option period, and he may confirm it. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'both have the option for three days or less' from Ibn Umar, from the Prophet (PBUH) who said: 'The two parties in a sale have the option in their sale as long as they have not separated or the sale is an option sale.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). Also the hadith to establish 'both have the option for three days or less' from Ibn Umar: 'The option is three days' (Darqutni, Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'the seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership' from Abu Hurairah: 'Do not separate from a sale except by mutual consent' (Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish 'if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand' - Shurayh said to Umar: 'You took it sound and safe, and you are liable for it until you return it sound and safe' (Baihaqi, Abd al-Razzaq). Principles: After offer and acceptance, it is permissible for the contracting parties to have the option to execute or cancel the sale. Principle: The sold item will not leave the seller's hand without his full consent. Then if he chooses confirmation in the absence of the other party, it is valid; and if he cancels, it is not valid unless the other is present. And when the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. And whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe, and he is contrary to that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes he may take him for the full price, and if he wishes he may leave him. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'if he chooses confirmation in the absence of the other party, it is valid' from Aisha: 'There is no harm or reciprocating harm' (Darqutni). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'when the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void' from Ibn Umar: 'The two parties in a sale each have the option against the other as long as they have not separated, except for an option sale' (Bukhari). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe' from Abu Hurairah: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade the sale of uncertainty and the sale of pebbles' (Tirmidhi). Evidence: (2) The hadith to establish 'whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe' from Ibn Umar: 'A man mentioned to the Prophet (PBUH) that he was deceived in sales, so he said: When you make a sale, say: No deception' (Bukhari). Principles: When the sale is completed, the price becomes obligatory. Principle: With the death of the desired object, the buyer gets the option to cancel the sale.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the option of stipulation (khayar al-shart) in the Hanafi matn of Al-Quduri, accompanied by hadith proofs and usul principles. The author first states the ruling: it is permissible for either party to stipulate an option period in a sale, with a maximum of three days according to Imam Abu Hanifa. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that any specified period is valid as long as it is known. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text then explains the legal effect of the seller's option: the seller retains ownership during the option period, so if the buyer takes possession and the item is destroyed, the buyer is liable for its value. The reasoning is that the seller has not fully consented to transfer ownership. For the buyer's option, there is consensus that ownership transfers from the seller, but Abu Hanifa says the buyer does not actually own it until he confirms, while the two students say he does own it. Thus, if the item perishes in the buyer's hands, under Abu Hanifa the buyer is liable for the value (since he didn't own it), but under Sahibayn he is liable for the price (since he owned it). The party with the option may either confirm or cancel the sale within the stipulated period. The text then provides hadith evidence for each point, including the famous hadith 'The option is three days' and the principle that sales require consent. On page 308, the text continues: if the option-holder confirms the sale in the absence of the other party, it is valid; but cancellation requires the other's presence, because cancellation is a dissolution of contract which needs mutual agreement. The death of the option-holder voids his option and it does not pass to heirs, because the option is a personal right attached to the living individual. Finally, if someone sells a slave described as having a specific skill (baker or scribe) and the description is false, the buyer has the option to either take the slave for the full price or return it. This is based on the prohibition of deceit and uncertainty in sales. The usul principles at the end emphasize that after offer and acceptance, the parties have the right to execute or cancel, and that the sold item cannot leave the seller's hand without his full consent.

Key Terms
ضمان بالقيمة (daman bi al-qima): Liability to pay the market value of the item if it is destroyed while in the possession of the buyer who does not own it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
During the seller's option, if the buyer takes possession and the item is destroyed, the buyer must pay:
A) The agreed price
B) The market value
C) Nothing
D) Half the price

Key Takeaway
Liability during khayar al-shart depends on whether the option belongs to the seller or buyer, and within the buyer's option, on the dispute over ownership: value per Abu Hanifa, price per Sahibayn.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
10 min
Exercising Khayar al-Shart: Confirmation, Cancellation, and Special Rulings
Rulings on exercising option and special cases with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rules for confirming or cancelling an option, the effect of the option-holder's death, and the buyer's option when a described attribute is absent, with their hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Confirmation is valid in absence; cancellation requires presence; option is personal and dies with holder; misdescription gives option to keep or return.

This lesson covers the procedural rules for exercising the option of stipulation. The passage from Al-Quduri outlines when confirmation and cancellation are valid, the effect of the option-holder's death, and a special case of sale with a described skill. These rulings are supported by hadith on mutual consent, prohibition of harm, and prohibition of deceit.

Guided Path
1
Analyze confirmation in absence
The option-holder can confirm the sale even if the other party is not present. This is valid because confirmation is a unilateral act that finalizes the contract.
Evidence: hadith 'لا ضرر ولا ضرار' indicates no harm in confirming without presence.
2
Analyze cancellation
Cancellation requires the other party's presence because it is a dissolution of the contract needing mutual consent. If the other is absent, cancellation is not valid.
This is because cancellation is a rescission, not a mere confirmation.
3
Examine death of the option-holder
If the one who has the option dies, the option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. The sale becomes binding immediately upon death.
Evidence: hadith 'الْمُتَبَايِعَانِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ عَلَى صَاحِبِهِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، إِلَّا بَيْعَ الخيار' indicates the option is personal to the living parties.
4
Examine misdescription
If someone sells a slave described as a baker or scribe, and the description is false, the buyer has the option to either take the slave for the full price or return him. This is based on the prohibition of deceit (gharar and tadlis).
Evidence: hadith forbidding gharar and the command to say 'la khilabah' (no deception).
5
Identify the underlying principles
The usul principles at the end emphasize that a completed sale fixes the price, and the death of the desired attribute gives the buyer an option to cancel.

بَابُ خِيَارِ الشَّرْطِ
قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ - خِيَارُ الشَّرْطِ جَائِزَ فِي الْبَيْعِ لِلْبَائِعِ وَالْمُشْتَرِي لَوَلَهُمَا الْخَيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا وَلا يَجُوزُ أَكْثَرُ مِنْهَا عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَجُوزُ إِذَا سَمَّيَا مُدَّةً مَعْلُومَةً وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمَنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيع مِنْ مِلْكِهِ فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ فِي مُدَّةِ الخيَارِ ضَمِنَهُ بِالْقِيمَةِ وَخِيَارُ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْك الْبَائِعِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ إِلَّا أَنَّ الْمُشْتَرِي لَا يَمْلِكُهُ عِندَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ وَمُحَمَّدٌ يَمْلِكُهُ فَإِنْ هَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ هَلَكَ بِالثَّمَنِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ دَخَلَهُ عَيْبٌ وَمَنْ شُرِطَ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ فَلَهُ أَنْ يَفْسَخَ فِي مُدَّةِ الْخِيَارِ وَلَهُ أَنْ يُجِيزَهُ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رضي الله عنهما، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «إِنَّ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ بِالْخِيَارِ فِي بَيْعِهِمَا مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا أَوْ يَكُونُ الْبَيْعُ خِيَارًا. »» (بخاري شريف بَابٌ كَمْ يَجُوزُ الْخِيَارُ ، نمبر 2107 / مسلم شريف: بَابٌ: كَمْ يَجُوزُ الْخِيَارُ،نمبر1531/(سنن ابوداود شريف، بَابٌ فِي خِيَارِ الْمُتَبَايِعَيْنِ، نمبر 3454) ل وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُمَا الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ فَمَا دُونَهَا \ عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْخِيَارُ ثَلَاثَةُ أَيَّامٍ» (سنن دار قطني، باب كتاب البيوع، نمبر3012 /سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي المُصَرَّاةِ، نمبر 1252) وجه: (١) الحديث لثبوت وَخِيَارُ الْبَائِعِ يَمْنَعُ خُرُوجَ الْمَبِيعِ مِنْ مِلْكِهِ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، عَنْ النَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «لَا يَتَفَرَّقَنَّ عَنْ بَيْعِ إِلَّا عَنْ تَرَاضٍ» (سنن الترمذي، باب، نمبر 1248) وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت فَإِذَا قَبَضَهُ الْمُشْتَرِي وَهَلَكَ فِي يَدِهِ \ فَقَالَ شُرَيْحٌ لِعُمَرَ: أَخَذْتَهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا وَأَنْتَ لَهُ ضَامِنٌ حَتَّى تَرُدَّهُ صَحِيحًا سَلِيمًا ، " ( السنن الكبري لليبيهقي، بَابُ الْمَأْخُوذِ عَلَى طَرِيقِ السَّوْمِ وَعَلَى بَيْعِ شُرِطَ فِيهِ الْخِيَارُ ، نمبر 10463/مصنف عبد الرزاق، باب: الرَّجُلُ يَشْتَرِي الشَّيْءَ عَلَى أَنْ يُجَرِّبَهُ فَيَهْلَكَ، غمبر 14978) اصول : ایجاب و قبول ہونے کے بعد متعاقدین کو بیچ کے نافذ کرنے یارد کرنے کا اختیار ہونا جائز ہے۔
اصول : بائع کی پوری رضامندی کے بغیر مبیع اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں نکلے گی۔
فَإِنْ اخْتَارَ الْإِجَازَةَ بِغَيْرِ حَضْرَةِ صَاحِبِهِ جَازَ وَإِنْ فَسَخَ لَمْ يَجْزَ إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ الْآخَرُ حَاضِرًا ك وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ بَطَلَ خِيَارُهُ وَلَمْ يَنْتَقِلْ إِلَى وَرَثَتِهِ
وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ فَكَانَ بِخِلَافِ ذَلِكَ فَالْمُشْتَرِي بِالخَيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ جَمِيعِ الثَّمَنِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ تَرَكَهُ
وجه : (1) الحديث لثبوت فَإِنْ اخْتَارَ الْإِجَازَةَ بِغَيْرِ حَضْرَةِ صَاحِبِهِ جَازَ \ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ ، ، قَالَ: «لَا ضَرَرَ وَلَا ضِرَارَ» (سنن دار قطني فِي الْمَرْأَةِ تُقْتَلُ إِذَا ارْتَدَّتْ، نمبر 4539) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَإِذَا مَاتَ مَنْ لَهُ الْخِيَارُ بَطَلَ خِيَارُهُ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي اللَّهُ عنهما: أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم قَالَ: «الْمُتَبَايِعَانِ كُلُّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمَا بِالْخِيَارِ عَلَى صَاحِبِهِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، إِلَّا بَيْعَ الخيار . » » (بخاري شريف بَابُ الْبَيْعَانِ بِالْخِيَارِ مَا لَمْ يَتَفَرَّقَا، نمبر 2111) وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازٌ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ \ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: «نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم عَنْ بَيْعِ الغَرَرِ، وَبَيْعِ الحَصَاةِ» (سنن الترمذي، بَابُ مَا جَاءَ فِي كَرَاهِيَةِ بَيْعِ الْغَرَرِ، غير (1230) وجه (۲) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ عَبْدًا عَلَى أَنَّهُ خَبَّازُ أَوْ كَاتِبٌ \ عَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِي الله عنهما: «أَنَّ رَجُلًا ذَكَرَ لِلنَّبِيِّ صلى الله عليه وسلم أَنَّهُ يُخْدَعُ فِي الْبُيُوعِ، فَقَالَ: إِذَا بَايَعْتَ فَقُلْ لَا خِلَابَةَ».»» (بخاري شريف بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ مِنَ الْخِدَاعِ فِي الْبَيْعِ، نمبر 2117) ه اصول : بیج مکمل ہو جائے تو شمن لازم ہو جاتا ہے۔
اصول : مفت مرغوب فیہ کے فوت ہونے سے مشتری کو بیچ توڑنے کا اختیار ہو گا۔
Chapter of the Option of Stipulation. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him - The option of stipulation is permissible in sale for the seller and the buyer, and both have the option for three days or less, and more than that is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: It is permissible if they specify a known period. The seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership; so if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand during the option period, he is liable for its value. The buyer's option does not prevent the sold item from leaving the seller's ownership by consensus, except that the buyer does not own it according to Abu Hanifa, and Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said he owns it. If it perishes in his hand, it perishes against the price, and likewise if a defect occurs in it. The one for whom the option is stipulated may cancel during the option period, and he may confirm it. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'both have the option for three days or less' from Ibn Umar, from the Prophet (PBUH) who said: 'The two parties in a sale have the option in their sale as long as they have not separated or the sale is an option sale.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud). Also the hadith to establish 'both have the option for three days or less' from Ibn Umar: 'The option is three days' (Darqutni, Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'the seller's option prevents the sold item from leaving his ownership' from Abu Hurairah: 'Do not separate from a sale except by mutual consent' (Tirmidhi). Evidence: (1) The saying of the Tabi'i to establish 'if the buyer takes possession and it perishes in his hand' - Shurayh said to Umar: 'You took it sound and safe, and you are liable for it until you return it sound and safe' (Baihaqi, Abd al-Razzaq). Principles: After offer and acceptance, it is permissible for the contracting parties to have the option to execute or cancel the sale. Principle: The sold item will not leave the seller's hand without his full consent. Then if he chooses confirmation in the absence of the other party, it is valid; and if he cancels, it is not valid unless the other is present. And when the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void and does not transfer to his heirs. And whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe, and he is contrary to that, the buyer has the option: if he wishes he may take him for the full price, and if he wishes he may leave him. Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'if he chooses confirmation in the absence of the other party, it is valid' from Aisha: 'There is no harm or reciprocating harm' (Darqutni). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'when the one who has the option dies, his option becomes void' from Ibn Umar: 'The two parties in a sale each have the option against the other as long as they have not separated, except for an option sale' (Bukhari). Evidence: (1) The hadith to establish 'whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe' from Abu Hurairah: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade the sale of uncertainty and the sale of pebbles' (Tirmidhi). Evidence: (2) The hadith to establish 'whoever sells a slave on the condition that he is a baker or a scribe' from Ibn Umar: 'A man mentioned to the Prophet (PBUH) that he was deceived in sales, so he said: When you make a sale, say: No deception' (Bukhari). Principles: When the sale is completed, the price becomes obligatory. Principle: With the death of the desired object, the buyer gets the option to cancel the sale.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the option of stipulation (khayar al-shart) in the Hanafi matn of Al-Quduri, accompanied by hadith proofs and usul principles. The author first states the ruling: it is permissible for either party to stipulate an option period in a sale, with a maximum of three days according to Imam Abu Hanifa. His two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that any specified period is valid as long as it is known. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The text then explains the legal effect of the seller's option: the seller retains ownership during the option period, so if the buyer takes possession and the item is destroyed, the buyer is liable for its value. The reasoning is that the seller has not fully consented to transfer ownership. For the buyer's option, there is consensus that ownership transfers from the seller, but Abu Hanifa says the buyer does not actually own it until he confirms, while the two students say he does own it. Thus, if the item perishes in the buyer's hands, under Abu Hanifa the buyer is liable for the value (since he didn't own it), but under Sahibayn he is liable for the price (since he owned it). The party with the option may either confirm or cancel the sale within the stipulated period. The text then provides hadith evidence for each point, including the famous hadith 'The option is three days' and the principle that sales require consent. On page 308, the text continues: if the option-holder confirms the sale in the absence of the other party, it is valid; but cancellation requires the other's presence, because cancellation is a dissolution of contract which needs mutual agreement. The death of the option-holder voids his option and it does not pass to heirs, because the option is a personal right attached to the living individual. Finally, if someone sells a slave described as having a specific skill (baker or scribe) and the description is false, the buyer has the option to either take the slave for the full price or return it. This is based on the prohibition of deceit and uncertainty in sales. The usul principles at the end emphasize that after offer and acceptance, the parties have the right to execute or cancel, and that the sold item cannot leave the seller's hand without his full consent.

Key Terms
خيار الشرط (khayar al-shart): An option stipulated in a sale contract allowing one or both parties to cancel or confirm the sale within a specified period.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the buyer with a khayar al-shart dies during the option period, what happens to the option?
A) It passes to the buyer's heirs.
B) It becomes void and the sale is binding.
C) The seller can decide.
D) The option extends by 3 days for the heirs.

Key Takeaway
Confirmation is valid without the other party's presence, but cancellation requires it; the option ends with death; false description gives the buyer an option to cancel or keep the item.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
15 min
Khiyar al-Ru'yah: The Buyer's Right to Inspect Unseen Goods
Rulings and proofs for the option of inspection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the option of inspection, identify the conditions that nullify it, and apply the ruling to cases of unseen purchases.

Core Idea
The buyer of an unseen item has the right to reject upon sight; the seller has no such option.

When a buyer purchases an item without seeing it, there is a natural risk of regret. The Hanafi school, drawing on prophetic hadith, grants the buyer a special right to inspect and either accept or reject the item upon seeing it. This lesson unpacks the rulings on khiyar al-ru'yah, including what constitutes sufficient inspection to extinguish the option, and how the rule applies to blind persons, real estate, and sales of another's property. We will also contrast the Hanafi position with that of Imam al-Shafi'i on selling what one does not possess.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fundamental rule
The author states that the buyer of an unseen item has the option of inspection; the seller does not. Note the asymmetry: the buyer is protected because he could not assess the item beforehand.
The seller is assumed to know his own goods; his regret is not acknowledged.
2
Examine the prophetic proof
The hadith of Abu Hurairah (marfu') explicitly grants the option: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' This is the primary textual evidence.
The hadith is ahad (single narrator chain), but accepted in Hanafi fiqh for establishing a non-obligatory right.
3
List what constitutes sufficient sight
Seeing the face of a heap, the outside of a folded cloth, the face of a slave girl or the face and hindquarters of an animal eliminates the option. Seeing the courtyard of a house suffices even without seeing rooms.
The principle: seeing the part that reveals the essential character of the item is enough.
4
Analyze special cases
For a blind person, touching, smelling, or tasting suffices if the item is known by those senses. For real estate, mere partial view is insufficient; a description is needed. The option falls upon the buyer's death.
These rulings are based on analogy (qiyas) and companion statements (athar).
5
Understand the dispute with al-Shafi'i
The Hanafi school upholds the validity of selling another's property without permission, giving the owner the option to ratify. The Shafi'i school, citing 'la bay' ma laysa 'indak', considers such sales void. Hanafis interpret the hadith differently.
The practical consequence: Hanafi law allows agents to sell goods they do not yet own, subject to ratification.

بَابُ الرُّؤْيَةِ بَابُ خِيَارِ الرُّؤْيَةِ قَالَ - رَحِمَهُ اللهُ - وَمَنْ اشْتَرَى مَا لَمْ يَرَهُ فَالْبَيْعُ جَائِزٌ وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِذَا رَآهُ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ وَإِنْ شَاءَ رَدَّهُ وَمَنْ بَاعَ مَا لَمْ يَرَهُ فَلَا خِيَارَ لَهُ وَمَنْ نَظَرَ إِلَى وَجْهِ الصُّبْرَةِ أَوْ إِلَى ظَاهِرِ التَّوْبِ مَطْوِيًّا أَوْ إِلَى وَجْهِ الْجَارِيَةِ أَوْ إِلَى وَجْهِ الدَّابَّةِ وَكِفْلِهَا فَلَا خِيَارَ لَهُ فَإِنْ رَأَى صَحْنَ الدَّارِ فَلَا خِيَارَ لَهُ وَإِنْ لَمْ يُشَاهِدْ بُيُوتَهَا وَبَيْعُ الْأَعْمَى وَشِرَاؤُهُ جَائِزٌ وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِذَا اشْتَرَى وَيَسْقُطُ خِيَارُهُ بِأَنْ يَجُسَّ الْمَبِيعَ إذَا كَانَ يُعْرَفُ بِالْجَسِّ أَوْ يَشُمَّهُ إِذَا كَانَ يُعْرَفُ بِالشَّمِّ أَوْ يَذُوقَهُ إِذَا كَانَ يُعْرَفُ بِالذَّوْقِ وَلَا يَسْقُطُ خِيَارُهُ فِي الْعَقَارِ حَتَّى يُوصَفَ لَهُ وَمَنْ بَاعَ مِلْكَ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ أَمْرِهِ فَالْمَالِكُ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شَاءَ أَجَازَ الْبَيْعَ وَإِنْ شَاءَ فَسَخَ وَلَهُ الْإِجَازَةُ إِذَا كَانَ الْمَعْقُودُ عَلَيْهِ بَاقِيًا وَالْمُتَعَاقِدَانِ بِحَالِهِمَا وَمَنْ رَأَى أَحَدَ التَّوْبَيْنِ فَاشْتَرَاهُمَا مَعًا ثُمَّ رَأَى الْآخَرَ جَازَ لَهُ أَنْ يَرُدَّهُمَا وَمَنْ مَاتَ وَلَهُ خِيَارُ رُؤْيَةٍ سَقَطَ خِيَارُهُ وَمَنْ رَأَى شَيْئًا ثُمَّ اشْتَرَاهُ بَعْدَ مُدَّةٍ فَإِنْ كَانَ عَلَى الصَّفَةِ الَّتِي رَآهَا فَلَا خِيَارَ لَهُ وَإِنْ وَجَدَهُ مُتَغَيِّرًا فَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِذَا رَآهُ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ وَإِنْ شَاءَ رَدَّهُ عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنِ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا لَمْ يَرَهُ فَهُوَ بِالْخِيَارِ إِذَا رَآهُ»
وجه : (۱) قول الصحابي لثبوت وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ إِذَا رَآهُ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ وَإِنْ شَاءَ رَدَّهُ عَنِ ابْنِ أَبِي مُلَيْكَةَ، أَنَّ عُثْمَانَ، ابْتَاعَ مِنْ طَلْحَةَ بْنِ عُبَيْدِ اللَّهِ أَرْضًا بِالْمَدِينَةِ نَاقَلَهُ بِأَرْضِ لَهُ بِالْكُوفَةِ فَلَمَّا تَبَايَعَا نَدِمَ عُثْمَانُ ثُمَّ قَالَ: " بَايَعْتُكَ مَا لَمْ أَرَهُ "، فَقَالَ طَلْحَةُ : " إِنَّمَا النَّظَرُ لِي إِنَّمَا ابْتَعْتُ مَغِيبًا "
وجه : (۱) الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ مِلْكَ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ أَمْرِهِ فَالْمَالِكُ بِالْخِيَارِ عَنْ عُرْوَةَ «أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ أَعْطَاهُ دِينَارًا يَشْتَرِي لَهُ بِهِ شَاةً فَاشْتَرَى لَهُ بِهِ شَاتَيْنِ فَبَاعَ إِحْدَاهُمَا بِدِينَارٍ وَجَاءَهُ بِدِينَارٍ وَشَاةٍ فَدَعَا لَهُ بِالْبَرَكَةِ فِي بَيْعِهِ وَكَانَ لَوِ اشْتَرَى التُّرَابَ لَرَبِحَ فِيهِ»
اصول : کسی شی کو بغیر دیکھے لیا تو خیر رویت حاصل ہو گی یعنی دیکھنے کے بعد چاہے تو لے یا رد کرے۔ اصول : مبیع کو دیکھنے سے پہلے مبیع سے راضی ہونے کا اعتبار نہیں ہے، البتہ رد کرنے کا حق ہے۔
وجه : (۱) دليل الشافعى الحديث لثبوت وَمَنْ بَاعَ مِلْكَ غَيْرِهِ بِغَيْرِ أَمْرِهِ فَالْمَالِكُ بِالْخِيَارِ اذَكَرَ عَبْدَ اللَّهِ بْنَ عَمْرٍو قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: «لا يَحِلُّ سَلَفٌ وَبَيْعٌ، وَلَا شَرْطَانِ فِي بَيْعٍ، وَلَا رِبْحُ مَا لَمْ تَضْمَنْ، وَلَا بَيْعُ مَا لَيْسَ عِنْدَكَ »
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ رَأَى أَحَدَ التَّوْبَيْنِ فَاشْتَرَاهُمَا مَعًا ثُمَّ رَأَى الْآخَرَ عَنِ الشَّعْبِيِّ فِي رَجُلٍ اشْتَرَى رَقِيقًا جُمْلَةً فَوَجَدَ بِبَعْضِهِمْ عَيْبًا قَالَ: «يَرُدُّهُمْ جَمِيعًا، أَوْ يَأْخُذُهُمْ جَمِيعًا»
وجه : (۱) قول التابعى لثبوت وَمَنْ رَأَى شَيْئًا ثُمَّ اشْتَرَاهُ بَعْدَ مُدَّةٍ عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ قَالَ: «إِذَا ابْتَاعَ رَجُلٌ مِنْكَ شَيْئًا عَلَى صِفَةٍ فَلَمْ تُخَالِفْ مَا وَصَفْتَ لَهُ فَقَدْ وَجَبَ عَلَيْهِ الْبَيْعُ»
اصول : مبیع کے جس حصہ کے دیکھنے سے مکمل دیکھنا مانا جاتا ہے، اس سے خیار رویت ساقط ہو گی۔ اصول : اصل پر قدرت نہ ہو تو نائب پر عمل کرنا کافی ہو گا، جس طرح وضو اور تیمم۔
Chapter of Ru'yah. Chapter of Khiyar al-Ru'yah. He (the author) said - may Allah have mercy on him -: Whoever buys what he has not seen, the sale is valid and he has the option when he sees it: if he wishes he takes it, and if he wishes he returns it. And whoever sells what he has not seen, there is no option for him. And whoever looks at the face of a heap, or at the outside of a folded cloth, or at the face of a slave girl, or at the face of an animal and its hindquarters, then there is no option for him. If he sees the courtyard of a house, then there is no option for him even if he did not see its rooms. The sale and purchase of a blind person are valid, and he has the option when he buys. His option falls by his touching the sold item if it is known by touch, or smelling it if it is known by smell, or tasting it if it is known by taste. And his option does not fall in real estate until it is described to him. And whoever sells the property of another without his permission, the owner has the option: if he wishes he ratifies the sale, and if he wishes he cancels it. And he may ratify provided the subject matter of the contract remains and the contracting parties are as they were. And whoever sees one of two cloths and buys both together, then sees the other, it is permissible for him to return both. And whoever dies having an option of inspection, his option falls. And whoever sees something then buys it after some time, then if it is upon the description he saw, there is no option for him, but if he finds it changed, he has the option. Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that he has the option when he sees it, if he wishes he takes it and if he wishes he returns it, from Abu Hurairah: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever buys something he has not seen, he has the option when he sees it.' Evidence: (1) The statement of a Companion for establishing that he has the option when he sees it, if he wishes he takes it and if he wishes he returns it, from Ibn Abi Mulaykah that Uthman bought land from Talhah ibn Ubaydullah in exchange for land of his in Kufah. When they had concluded the transaction, Uthman regretted and said: 'I sold you what I have not seen.' Talhah said: 'The option is for me; I bought an absent property.' Evidence: (1) The hadith for establishing that whoever sells the property of another without his permission, the owner has the option, from Urwah: The Prophet gave him a dinar to buy a sheep for him, so he bought two sheep with it and sold one of them for a dinar, and came to him with a dinar and a sheep. He prayed for blessing for him in his trade, and if he had bought dust he would have profited. Principle: When something is taken without seeing it, the option of inspection is obtained, meaning after seeing, if he wishes he takes it or returns it. Principle: Before seeing the sold item, satisfaction with the sold item is not considered; however, there is the right to return. Evidence: (1) The proof of al-Shafi'i, the hadith for establishing that whoever sells the property of another without his permission, the owner has the option: It was narrated by Abdullah ibn Amr that the Messenger of Allah said: 'A loan and a sale are not permissible, nor two conditions in a sale, nor profit without liability, nor selling what is not with you.' Evidence: (1) The statement of a Tabi'i for establishing that whoever sees one of two cloths and buys both together then sees the other, from al-Sha'bi concerning a man who bought slaves in a lot and found a defect in some of them: he said: 'He returns them all or takes them all.' Evidence: (1) The statement of a Tabi'i for establishing that whoever sees something then buys it after some time, from Ibn Sirin who said: 'When a man buys something from you based on a description, and you do not contradict what you described to him, then the sale is binding upon him.' Principle: Seeing that part of the sold item through which complete seeing is considered, the option of inspection falls. Principle: When power over the original is not possible, then acting through the deputy is sufficient, like in wudu and tayammum.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a combined matn and sharh from Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and its commentary on the chapter of Khiyar al-Ru'yah (Option of Inspection). The author begins by stating the fundamental rule: a buyer who purchases an unseen item has the right to inspect it upon seeing and either accept or reject the sale. This is a concession to protect the buyer from regret, and it is established by the hadith of Abu Hurairah (marfu'). The seller, however, has no such option because he is the one who offered the item. The text then details what constitutes sufficient seeing to nullify the option: looking at the face of a heap or the outside of a folded cloth, or the face of a slave girl or animal, eliminates the option because these reveal the essential characteristics. Similarly, seeing the courtyard of a house suffices even without seeing the rooms. For a blind person, the option falls by using other senses (touch, smell, taste) if the item is typically recognized that way. Real estate requires a description for the option to fall, not just seeing part of it. When someone sells another's property without permission, the owner has the option to ratify or cancel, provided the subject matter and parties remain unchanged. This ruling is supported by the hadith of Urwah about the Prophet's transaction. The commentary also addresses a Shafi'i proof (the hadith 'La yahillu salaf wa bay'... ) which is used by Shafi'is to argue against selling what one does not possess; however, the Hanafi school interprets it differently and upholds the validity of such sales with the option. The principles (usul) extracted are: (1) The option of inspection is established for the buyer who purchases unseen; (2) Pre-purchase satisfaction is not binding; and (3) When direct inspection is impossible, the equivalent method (touch/smell/description) suffices. The ruling that the option falls upon the buyer's death is stated, following the principle that options are not inheritable in this case.

Key Terms
خِيَارُ الرُّؤْيَةِ (khiyar al-ru'yati): The right of the buyer of an unseen item to accept or reject it after seeing it.
صُبْرَة (subrah): A heap or pile (e.g., of grain) whose face (surface) is seen; seeing the face suffices to eliminate the option.
مَطْوِيًّا (matwiyyan): Folded; referring to cloth that is folded, so seeing the outside is considered sufficient sight.
مَوْقُوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract that is valid but contingent on a third party's ratification (e.g., sale of another's property).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a blind person purchases an item and then recognizes it by touching it?
A) The option of inspection remains because he cannot see.
B) The option falls because he recognized it by touch.
C) The sale is invalid because a blind person cannot contract.
D) The option falls only if he described the item to him.

Key Takeaway
The buyer of an unseen item has a right to inspect and reject, but this right is extinguished by sufficient sight or its equivalent, and the seller has no such right.

Buyu — Sales and Trade
intermediate
8 min
The Hanafi Ruling on Option of Defect (Khiyar al-Ayb)
Quduri's matn on khiyar al-ayb with hadith proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the buyer's options upon discovering a defect and apply the Hanafi definition of 'ayb based on custom.

Core Idea
The buyer may keep the item or return it — no partial refund.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-ayb (option of defect) as presented in Al-Quduri's matn. The key principle is that the buyer has a binary choice: accept the item at full price or return it for a full refund. A partial refund while keeping the item is impermissible. This ruling is derived from the prophetic hadith 'Profit is with liability' (al-kharaj bi al-daman) and is supported by the practice of the early generations. The lesson also defines what constitutes a defect ('ayb) according to trade custom and addresses scenarios where the buyer causes a new defect.

Guided Path
1
Identify the buyer's core options
Read the first sentence of the matn: the buyer, upon discovering a defect, may either keep the item at the full price or return it. Note what is explicitly prohibited: demanding a reduction while keeping the item.
This is the central rule of khiyar al-ayb in the Hanafi school.
2
Define 'ayb (defect) according to Hanafi fiqh
The matn defines 'ayb as 'everything that necessitates a reduction in price in the custom of merchants.' This is a custom-based ('urfi) definition. The examples given (running away, bedwetting, stealing in a minor, halitosis) illustrate the principle but do not limit it.
The Shafi'i school has a more fixed definition; Hanafis rely on merchant custom.
3
Analyze the primary proof: hadith al-kharaj bi al-daman
The hadith 'Profit is with liability' (الخراج بالضمان) is cited. Understand its implication: since the buyer enjoyed the profit/use of the item, he must bear the risk of loss. Therefore, he cannot get a partial refund; he either takes full responsibility (keeps) or relinquishes all benefit (returns).
This is an ahad hadith, but it is accepted in Hanafi usul as zanni al-thubut yet sufficient for establishing a ruling.
4
Apply the rule when a new defect occurs after purchase
If the buyer causes a new defect (e.g., cuts the cloth, sews it into a shirt) before discovering the original defect, he loses the right to return the item. Instead, he can claim compensation for the reduction caused by the original defect. The seller cannot force a return.
This is a key practical exception: the right to return is lost if the item is altered or a new defect is introduced by the buyer.
5
Distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position
The matn implies that the buyer cannot demand a partial refund. This is a point of ikhtilaf: the Shafi'i school allows the buyer to keep the item and claim the difference in value. The Hanafi school restricts the option to either full return or full acceptance.
The difference stems from interpreting the hadith and the role of liability (daman).
