Adding Expenses to Capital in Murabahah
Provides ruling on including costs like tailoring and carriage in the capital sum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on adding customary post-purchase expenses to the capital in Murabahah and identify the required truthful disclosure wording.

Core Idea
Customary expenses may be added to capital in Murabahah, but seller must say 'it cost me', not 'I bought it for'.

This lesson examines a clear ruling from al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on the permissibility of including certain post-purchase costs (like tailoring, dyeing, and carriage) in the capital sum of a Murabahah sale. The key principle is honesty in disclosure: the seller must truthfully state the total cost, not misrepresent it as the original purchase price. Understanding this ruling helps avoid gharar and falsehood in credit sales.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What action is being permitted? Adding certain post-purchase expenses to the capital sum (ra's al-mal) in a Murabahah transaction.
2
List the covered expenses
Note the specific expenses mentioned: wage of fuller, dyer, embroiderer, twister, and carriage charge for food. These are customary value-adding costs.
The list is illustrative; other similar customary expenses are also included.
3
Recognize the linguistic condition
The seller must say 'qāma 'alayya bi-kadhā' (it cost me such-and-such), not 'ishtaraytuhu bi-kadhā' (I bought it for such-and-such). The latter would be false because the total cost includes post-purchase expenses.
Truthfulness is essential for the validity of the Murabahah contract.
4
Acknowledge the proof
The ruling is supported by a statement from the Tabi'i Ibrahim al-Nakha'i, who permitted this practice when asked about adding fulling and rent to the purchase price.
This is recorded in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah.
5
Understand the scope and limitation
Not all expenses can be added; only those that are customary and increase the value of the goods. Expenses must be actual and not arbitrary.
The common misunderstanding is that any expense can be added arbitrarily.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُضِيفَ إِلَى رَأْسِ الْمَالِ أُجْرَةَ الْقَصَّارِ وَالصَّبَّاغِ وَالطَّرَّازِ وَالْفَتَالِ وَأُجْرَةَ حَمْلِ الطَّعَامِ، وَيَقُولُ قَامَ عَلَيَّ بِكَذَا، وَلَا يَقُولُ اشْتَرَيْتُهُ بِكَذَا.
وَجْهٌ (١) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ أَنْ يُضِيفَ...: قُلْتُ لِإِبْرَاهِيمَ إِنَّا نَشْتَرِي الْمَتَاعَ ثُمَّ نَزِيدُ عَلَيْهِ الْقَصَارَةَ وَالْكِرَاءَ، ثُمَّ نَبِيعُهُ بِدَهْيَازُدَهُ، قَالَ: «لَا بَأْسَ». (مصنف ابن أبي شيبة في النفقة تضم إلى رأس المال، رقم 20411)
And it is permissible to add to the capital the wage of the fuller, the dyer, the embroiderer, the twister, and the carriage charge of food, and he says 'it cost me such-and-such', and he does not say 'I bought it for such-and-such'. Proof (1): Statement of the Tabi'i to establish that it is permissible to add...: I said to Ibrahim: We buy goods then add to it the fuller's fee and the rent, then we sell it for eleven. He said: 'No problem.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, chapter on expenses added to capital, number 20411)
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This ruling_statement from the matn allows the seller in a Murabahah to include post-purchase expenses (like tailoring, dyeing, embroidery, twisting, and carriage) in the capital sum disclosed to the buyer. However, the seller must be honest: he should say 'it cost me such-and-such', not 'I bought it for such-and-such', because the latter would be false. The proof is a statement from Ibrahim al-Nakha'i (a Tabi'i) who permitted this practice.

Key Terms
أُجْرَةُ الْقَصَّارِ (ujrat al-qaṣṣār): Wage of the fuller (one who cleans and presses cloth).
رَأْسُ الْمَالِ (raʾs al-māl): The capital sum or original cost of the goods.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 'I paid such-and-such including expenses'
D) 'The price is such-and-such'

Key Takeaway
In Murabahah, specified customary expenses may be added to the capital sum, but the seller must honestly state the total cost, not the original purchase price.

Fraud in Murabahah and Tawliyah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Buyer's Remedy
Presents Abu Hanifa's ruling on fraud and the ikhtilaf of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on buyer's option upon discovering fraud in Murabahah and Tawliyah, and distinguish the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
In Murabahah, fraud gives an option; in Tawliyah, only deduction — but the Sahibayn disagreed.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: what remedy does the buyer have when a seller commits fraud in disclosing the cost price? Imam Abu Hanifa distinguished between Murabahah (profit declared) and Tawliyah (cost-only). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) each held uniform rules, leading to three distinct positions. Understanding this ikhtilaf sharpens your ability to apply the school's principles of khiyar and amanah.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling for each contract type: in Murabahah, buyer has option to take at full price or return; in Tawliyah, buyer deducts the fraud from the price.
2
Identify the opposing views within the school
Note that Abu Yusuf holds: deduction in both. Muhammad holds: option in both.
3
Locate the proofs
The passage cites a hadith against fraud. The underlying rationale distinguishes the nature of the contracts: Tawliyah is pure trust (amanah), Murabahah involves a profit statement.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: in Murabahah, following Abu Hanifa, buyer can return the item or pay full price; following Abu Yusuf, he only deducts; following Muhammad, he also has the option.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view in the school is Abu Hanifa's, as recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا اطَّلَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي عَلَى خِيَانَةٍ فِي الْمُرَابَحَةِ فَهُوَ بِالْخِيَارِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ إِنْ شَاءَ أَخَذَهُ بِجَمِيعِ الثَّمَنِ، وَإِنْ شَاءَ رَدَّهُ. وَإِنِ اطَّلَعَ عَلَى خِيَانَةٍ فِي التَّوْلِيَةِ أَسْقَطَهَا مِنَ الثَّمَنِ.
وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ: يَحُطُّ فِيهِمَا. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: لَا يَحُطُّ فِيهِمَا وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ.
وَجْهٌ: الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَإِذَا اطَّلَعَ الْمُشْتَرِي عَلَى خِيَانَةٍ فِي الْمُرَابَحَةِ: عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ، عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ: «ثَلَاثَةٌ لَا يَنْظُرُ اللَّهُ إِلَيْهِمْ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ، وَلَا يُزَكِّيهِمْ، وَلَهُمْ عَذَابٌ أَلِيمٌ». قُلْنَا: مَنْ هُمْ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، فَقَدْ خَابُوا وَخَسِرُوا؟ فَقَالَ: «الْمَنَّانُ، وَالْمُسْبِلُ إِزَارَهُ، وَالْمُنَفِّقُ سِلْعَتَهُ بِالْخَلِفِ الْكَاذِبِ». (سنن الترمذي، باب ما جاء فيمن حلف على سلعة كاذبا، رقم 1211)
And if the buyer discovers fraud in Murabahah, he has an option according to Abu Hanifa: if he wishes, he takes it at the full price, and if he wishes, he returns it. And if he discovers fraud in Tawliyah, he deducts it from the price. Abu Yusuf said: He deducts in both. Muhammad said: He does not deduct in both, and he has the option. Proof: Hadith to establish when the buyer discovers fraud in Murabahah: from Abu Dharr, from the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) who said: 'Three people Allah will not look at on the Day of Resurrection, nor will He purify them, and they will have a painful punishment.' We said: Who are they, O Messenger of Allah? They have indeed failed and lost. He said: 'The one who reminds others of his favors, the one who trails his garment, and the one who sells his goods by false oath.' (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, chapter on one who takes a false oath on a commodity, number 1211)
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (intra_hanafi_dispute). Abu Hanifa distinguishes between Murabahah and Tawliyah: in Murabahah, the buyer can either accept the sale at the full price or return it (option of revocation); in Tawliyah, the buyer simply deducts the amount of fraud from the price. Abu Yusuf holds that in both cases the buyer deducts the fraud; Muhammad holds that in both cases the buyer has the option (not deduction). The proof cited is a general hadith against fraud in sales, which supports that fraudulent conduct is prohibited, though the specific options are based on the nature of the contract.

Key Terms
خِيَانَةٌ (khiyānah): Fraud or dishonesty in disclosing the true cost.
الْخِيَارُ (al-khiyār): Option: the right to either uphold or rescind the contract.
حَطَّ (ḥaṭṭa): To deduct or reduce the price.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what happens if the buyer discovers fraud in a Tawliyah sale?
A) He may return the item.
B) He deducts the fraud from the price.
C) He must pay the full price.
D) He has no remedy.

Key Takeaway
The buyer's remedy upon fraud depends on the contract type: Murabahah gives a return option, Tawliyah gives a price deduction, per the school's relied-upon view.

Selling Before Possession: General Rule and Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Real Estate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling real estate before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on selling movables before possession and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding real estate, including the proofs and the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Selling before possession is prohibited for movables; for real estate, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf allow it, but Muhammad forbids it.

In Hanafi fiqh, the rule that a buyer cannot sell an item before taking possession is firmly established for movable goods. However, a significant intra-madhhab dispute exists regarding real estate: the majority of the school permits it, while Imam Muhammad considers it impermissible. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the practical consequence of this difference.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule for movable goods
Read the opening sentence: 'Whoever buys something that is movable and transportable, it is not permissible for him to sell it until he takes possession of it.' Identify the ruling: selling before possession is not allowed (la yajuz).
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on real estate
Note the two positions: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit selling real estate before possession; Muhammad does not. Highlight that this is a disagreement within the same school.
3
Examine the proofs for the general rule
The text cites the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar specifically mentioning food. The Hanafi school extends the prohibition to all movables by qiyas, but not to real estate.
The hadith text is from Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Analyze the proofs for the real estate dispute
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rely on the specificity of the hadith (food only) and the practice of the Tabi'un (Ibn Sirin's statement). Muhammad argues that real estate is also a commodity and the prohibition should apply by analogy.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and its practical effect
The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: selling real estate before possession is permissible. The practical difference is whether one can immediately resell a purchased house without waiting for possession.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنِ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا مِمَّا يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوَّلُ لَمْ يَجُزْ لَهُ بَيْعُهُ حَتَّى يَقْبِضَهُ. وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْعَقَارِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: لَا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْعَقَارِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ.
وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَمَنِ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا...: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: «أَمَّا الَّذِي نَهَى عَنْهُ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ فَهُوَ الطَّعَامُ أَنْ يُبَاعَ حَتَّى يُقْبَضَ». (بخاري، باب بيع الطعام قبل أن يقبض)
وَجْهٌ (٢) الْحَدِيثُ: عَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: «مَنِ ابْتَاعَ طَعَامًا فَلَا يَبِعْهُ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِيَهُ». زَادَ إِسْمَاعِيلُ: «حَتَّى يَقْبِضَهُ». (بخاري، مسلم، سنن أبي داود)
وَجْهٌ (١) الْحَدِيثُ لِثُبُوتِ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْعَقَارِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ...: سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: «أَمَّا الَّذِي نَهَى عَنْهُ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ فَهُوَ الطَّعَامُ أَنْ يُبَاعَ حَتَّى يُقْبَضَ». (بخاري)
وَجْهٌ (٢) قَوْلُ التَّابِعِيِّ: عَنِ ابْنِ سِيرِينَ قَالَ: «لَا بَأْسَ أَنْ يَشْتَرِيَ شَيْئًا لَا يُكَالُ وَلَا يُوزَنُ بِنَقْدٍ، ثُمَّ يَبِيعَهُ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَقْبِضَهُ». (مصنف عبد الرزاق)
أُصُولٌ: مَنْقُولَ اشْیَاء پر قبضہ کئے بغیر آگے بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے نبی کے فرمان "فَلَا یَبِیعَهُ حَتَّى یَقْبِضَهُ" کی وجہ سے۔
And whoever buys something that is movable and transportable, it is not permissible for him to sell it until he takes possession of it. And it is permissible to sell real estate before possession according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. And Muhammad said: It is not permissible to sell real estate before possession. Proof (1): Hadith to establish 'whoever buys something...': I heard Ibn Abbas (radiallahu anhuma) say: 'What the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) forbade is food that it be sold until it is taken possession of.' (Bukhari, chapter on selling food before taking possession) Proof (2): Hadith: from Ibn Umar (radiallahu anhuma): that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) said: 'Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he takes delivery of it.' Ismail added: 'until he takes possession of it.' (Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud) Proof (1) for permissibility of selling real estate before possession according to Abu Hanifa...: Ibn Abbas said: ... Proof (2): Statement of the Tabi'i: from Ibn Sirin who said: 'There is no harm in buying something that is not measured or weighed by cash, then selling it before taking possession.' (Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq) Principle: Selling movable things before taking possession is not permissible because of the Prophet's command 'do not sell it until he takes possession of it.'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage contains two rulings: (1) Movable goods (manqul) cannot be sold before the buyer takes possession, based on the hadith prohibiting sale of food before possession. (2) For real estate (aqar), there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit selling before possession by analogy with services, while Muhammad forbids it by analogy with movables. The proofs include hadith from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar, and a statement from Ibn Sirin allowing non-food items. The Urdu summary reiterates the principle.

Key Terms
يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوَّلُ (yunqalu wa yuḥawwal): Movable and transportable goods.
الْعَقَارُ (al-ʿaqār): Real estate (immovable property).
الْقَبْضُ (al-qabḍ): Physical or constructive possession (taking delivery).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative) Hanafi position, which of the following is true regarding selling real estate before taking possession?
A) It is permissible, as stated by Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
B) It is not permissible, as stated by Muhammad al-Shaybani.
C) It is permissible only if the price is paid in full.
D) It is likened to selling food before possession and thus prohibited.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits selling movables before possession based on hadith, but permits selling real estate before possession according to the majority view, with Imam Muhammad dissenting.

Buyu — Sales and Trade

Requirement to Remeasure or Reweigh When Selling by Quantity
Ruling that goods sold by measure/weight must be remeasured/reweighed before resale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that a buyer must remeasure goods bought by measure before reselling by measure, and identify the Quranic proof supporting this ruling.

Core Idea
A buyer must remeasure goods bought by measure before reselling; the original measure does not carry over.

When you buy a commodity by measurement or weight, you become its owner and are free to use or resell it. However, if you wish to resell it by the same method (measure or weight), you cannot simply rely on the original measurement. This lesson explains the legal requirement to remeasure or reweigh for the second buyer, drawing on a clear Quranic principle against cheating in trade.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is purchasing a measured commodity and then reselling it by measure. The ruling: it is not permissible (lam yajuz) to sell, dispose, or consume until the measure is repeated.
This applies only when both purchase and resale are by measure/weight; if sold by sight, different rules apply.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Quran 83:2-3, which condemns those who give less when measuring or weighing for others.
The verse is general but applied here to require full measure in every transaction.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse implies that giving full measure is obligatory. By requiring remeasuring, the new buyer receives the full quantity they are entitled to, preventing fraud.
The prohibition of under-measuring implies the duty to over-measure? Actually the duty is to give exactly as agreed.
4
Note the consequence
If the buyer resells without remeasuring, the sale is fasid (corrupt) and must be rectified.
Some later Hanafi texts clarify that the second sale is suspended until remeasuring.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنِ اشْتَرَى مَكِيلًا مُكَايَلَةً أَوْ مَوْزُونًا مُوَازَنَةً فَاكْتَالَهُ أَوِ اتَّزَنَهُ، ثُمَّ بَاعَهُ مُكَايَلَةً أَوْ مُوَازَنَةً لَمْ يَجُزْ لِلْمُشْتَرِي مِنْهُ أَنْ يَبِيعَهُ وَلَا يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيهِ وَلَا يَأْكُلَهُ حَتَّى يُعِيدَ الْكَيْلَ أَوِ الْوَزْنَ فِيهِ ثَانِيًا.
وَجْهٌ: الْأَيَةُ لِثُبُوتِ ذَلِكَ: ﴿الَّذِينَ إِذَا اكْتَالُوا عَلَى النَّاسِ يَسْتَوْفُونَ، وَإِذَا كَالُوهُمْ أَوْ وَزَنُوهُمْ يُخْسِرُونَ﴾ (سورة المطففين، الآيتان 2-3)
And whoever buys a measured commodity by measure, or a weighed commodity by weight, and then measures it or weighs it, then sells it by measure or weight, it is not permissible for the buyer from him to sell it, nor to dispose of it, nor to eat it, until he repeats the measure or weight a second time. Proof: The verse to establish that: 'Those who, when they take a measure from people, take full measure, and when they measure for them or weigh for them, they give less.' (Surah al-Mutaffifin, verses 2-3)
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This ruling_with_proof states that when a commodity is bought by measurement or weight, and then the buyer wishes to resell it by the same method (measure or weight), he must remeasure or reweigh it for the second buyer. He cannot rely on the original measurement or weight. This is because the property has transferred, and the new buyer is entitled to an honest measure/weight. The proof is from Surah al-Mutaffifin, which condemns cheating in measurement and weight, implying that proper measurement is obligatory in each transaction.

Key Terms
مَكِيلٌ (makīl): A commodity sold by measurement (e.g., grain).
مُكَايَلَةً (mukāyalatan): A sale based on measurement.
إِعَادَةُ الْكَيْلِ (iʿādat al-kayl): Repeating the measurement for the subsequent buyer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a buyer do before selling a measured item by measure that he bought by measure?
A) He can sell it based on the original measurement.
B) He must remeasure it for the new buyer.
C) He does not need to do anything if the container is sealed.
D) He can estimate the quantity.

Key Takeaway
Remeasuring or reweighing before resale by measure/weight is wajib to ensure honest trade, as demanded by the Quran.

Selling Before Possession and the Exception for Real Estate
Intra-Hanafi dispute on selling real estate before possession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on selling movable goods before possession, distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding real estate, and apply the hadith proofs to justify the exception for real estate.

Core Idea
Selling movable goods before possession is invalid; real estate is an exception per Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, based on hadith limiting prohibition to food.

This passage from Al-Quduri addresses a key practical issue: can you sell something you just bought before you physically take it? The general rule is clear for movable goods, but a dispute arises over real estate. Two hadiths from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar explicitly mention only food, which Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf use to permit selling real estate before possession. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, extending the prohibition by analogy. We will examine the proofs and determine the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule on selling movables before possession
Identify that the text clearly prohibits selling movable items until possession is taken. This is the default ruling for all goods that can be physically moved.
Movables include any item that can be transferred, e.g., cars, clothes, food.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute on real estate
Note that real estate (land, buildings) has a different treatment. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit selling it before possession; Muhammad prohibits it. Recognize this as an ikhtilaf within the school.
The dispute is based on how to interpret the hadiths and whether analogy (qiyas) applies.
3
Analyze the hadith proofs and their scope
Examine the two hadiths quoted. Both explicitly mention 'food' (ta'am). Abu Hanifa argues that this specific mention limits the prohibition to food only, so other items like real estate are not included. This is a key textual basis for the exception.
The word 'طعام' is used in both hadiths, indicating the prohibition is confined to food.
4
Examine Muhammad's opposing qiyas argument
Muhammad uses analogy: since food is prohibited because of risk of loss before possession, the same reasoning applies to real estate, which also carries risk (e.g., fire, flood). Thus, he extends the prohibition to real estate.
The 'illa (effective cause) according to Muhammad is the possibility of loss before full transfer.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position and its basis
The Hanafi school follows Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The relied-upon fatwa is that real estate can be sold before possession. This is based on the explicit wording of the hadiths and customary practice ('urf) considering real estate as fixed and less risky.
This view is supported by the majority of Hanafi scholars and is the operative position for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَابُ الْمُرَاحَةِ وَالتَّوْلِيَةِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ يَحُطُّ فِيهِمَا وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: لَا يَحُطُّ فِيهِمَا وَلَهُ الْخِيَارُ وَمَنْ اشْتَرَى شَيْئًا مِمَّا يُنْقَلُ وَيُحَوَّلُ لَمْ يَجُزْ لَهُ بَيْعُهُ حَتَّى يَقْبِضَهُ وَيَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْعَقَارِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ عِنْدَ أَبي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبي يُوسُفَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ لا يَجُوزُ بَيْعُ الْعَقَارِ قَبْلَ الْقَبْضِ . سَمِعْتُ ابْنَ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا يَقُولُ: أَمَّا الَّذِي نَهَى عَنْهُ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَهُوَ الطَّعَامُ أَنْ يُبَاعَ حَتَّى يُقْبَضَ. وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: مَنِ ابْتَاعَ طَعَامًا فَلَا يَبِعْهُ حَتَّى يَسْتَوْفِيَهُ. وَزَادَ إِسْمَاعِيلُ: مَنِ ابْتَاعَ طَعَامًا فَلَا يَبِعْهُ حَتَّى يَقْبِضَهُ.
Chapter of Murabahah and Tawliyah. Abu Yusuf said: He discounts in both. Muhammad said: He does not discount in both, and he has the option. Whoever buys something that is movable and transferable, it is not permissible for him to sell it until he takes possession of it. And sale of real estate before possession is permissible according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: Sale of real estate before possession is not permissible. I heard Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them both, saying: 'What the Prophet, peace be upon him, forbade is food being sold until it is taken possession of.' And from Ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them both, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he receives it in full.' And Isma'il added: 'Whoever buys food, let him not sell it until he takes possession of it.'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on Murabahah and Tawliyah (types of sale with profit disclosure). The first part records an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf holds that the seller may discount (yahuṭṭu) the profit or price in these transactions, while Muhammad holds that he may not discount but the buyer has the option to proceed or cancel. The main ruling then addresses selling before possession (qabd). The general rule is that selling movable (manqul) goods before the buyer has taken physical possession is invalid. However, for real estate ('aqar), Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf permit selling before possession, based on custom and the specific wording of the hadith that only mentions food. Muhammad disagrees and extends the prohibition to real estate by analogy (qiyas). The two hadith proofs (from Ibn Abbas and Ibn Umar) explicitly restrict the prohibition to food, thus supporting Abu Hanifa's exception for real estate. The hadith from Ibn Abbas states that the Prophet's prohibition was specifically about food, implying other items like real estate are not included. The second hadith from Ibn Umar uses 'food' as well. Thus, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that real estate can be sold before possession, following Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Key Terms
المراحبة (al-murabahah): A sale where the seller discloses the cost price and adds a known profit margin.
التولية (al-tawliyah): A sale where the seller transfers the goods at the same cost price without profit.
القبض (al-qabd): Taking physical or constructive possession of the purchased item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the relied-upon position regarding selling real estate before taking possession?
A) It is prohibited, following the analogy to movable goods.
B) It is permissible, because the hadith prohibition is limited to food.
C) It is makruh tanzihi but valid.
D) It is only permissible if the seller gives the buyer the option.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits selling real estate before possession because the prophetic prohibition in the hadiths is specifically confined to food, making it an exception to the general rule requiring possession before resale.

Selling Pre-Measured Goods: Why Remeasurement is Required
States ruling with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding remeasurement when selling measured/weighed goods and apply it to a given scenario.

Core Idea
Each sale of measured/weighed goods requires its own measurement; the same measurement cannot be reused.

Imagine you buy a sack of wheat, measure it, then later want to sell it to someone else by weight. Does the original weighing suffice? The Hanafi school says no—you must weigh it again for the new buyer. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its Quranic and Prophetic proofs, and the rationale behind the requirement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
First, note that the commodity is makil (sold by volume) or mawzun (sold by weight). The ruling is that the buyer who has already measured/weighed it cannot sell, dispose, or consume it until he measures/weighs it again for the new transaction.
The ruling applies only if the subsequent sale is also by measure/weight, not if sold by lump sum.
2
Locate the Legal Proof (Dalil)
Two proofs are cited: Quran 83:1-3 condemning cheating in measurement, and the Prophet's command 'When you sell, measure; when you buy, measure.' Identify each proof and its source.
The hadith is reported by Uthman and found in Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Analyze the Proof (Wajh al-Dalalah)
The imperative 'kil' (measure) in the hadith indicates obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The verse implies that accurate measurement is a requirement for justice in transactions. Thus, each sale requires its own measurement.
The dalala of the Quranic verse is zanni when applied to this specific ruling, but the hadith is clear.
4
Determine the Scope and Exceptions
If the second sale is by lump sum (juzafan), where the quantity is not specified, then remeasurement is not required. The ruling is limited to sales where the quantity is a determining factor.
This exception is based on the principle that juzaf sale is valid even if the exact quantity is unknown, as long as the parties are satisfied.
5
Apply the Ruling to a Scenario
Given a scenario (e.g., someone buys rice by weight, weighs it, then wants to sell a portion by weight), decide whether remeasurement is required and state the consequence if it is not done.
If remeasurement is omitted, the sale is fasid (corrupt) until the quantity is determined.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ اشْتَرَى مَكِيلًا مُكَايَلَةً أَوْ مَوْزُونَا مُوَازَنَةً فَاكْتَالَهُ أَوْ اتَّزَنَهُ ثُمَّ بَاعَهُ مُكَايَلَةً أَوْ مُوَازَنَةً لَمْ يَجُزْ لِلْمُشْتَرِي مِنْهُ أَنْ يَبِيعَهُ وَلَا يَتَصَرَّفَ فِيهِ وَلَا يَأْكُلَهُ حَتَّى يُعِيدَ الْكَيْلَ أَوْ الْوَزْنَ فِيهِ ثَانِيًا. ﴿الَّذِينَ إِذَا اكْتَالُوا عَلَى النَّاسِ يَسْتَوْفُونَ . وَإِذَا كَالُوهُمْ أَوْ وَّزَنُوهُمْ يُخْسِرُونَ﴾. وَعَنْ عُثْمَانَ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: إِذَا بِعْتَ فَكِلْ وَإِذَا ابْتَعْتَ فَاكْتَل.
Whoever buys something that is measured by measure or weighed by weight, and he measures it or weighs it, then sells it by measure or weight, it is not permissible for the buyer from him to sell it, nor to dispose of it, nor to eat it until he repeats the measure or weight in it a second time. (Quran) 'Those who, when they take measure from people, take full measure, and when they give measure or weight, give less.' And from Uthman, may Allah be pleased with him, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'When you sell, then measure; and when you buy, then measure.'
Source pages p. 325

Commentary
This passage presents a specific ruling related to the sale of goods sold by measure or weight. If a person buys a commodity that is customarily measured (makil) or weighed (mawzun), and he actually performs the measurement or weighing himself (e.g., the seller delivers it, and the buyer measures it), then if he wants to sell that same commodity again by measure or weight, he must remeasure or reweigh it for the new buyer. The original measurement was performed for the first transaction; it does not suffice for the second. The reason is that measurement/weight is a means of determining the quantity for each contract, and the buyer must ensure the exact amount for the subsequent buyer. The Quranic verse (Surah al-Mutaffifin) condemns those who cheat in measurement, implying the importance of accurate measurement. The hadith from Uthman instructs to measure when selling and measuring when buying, indicating that each transaction requires its own measurement. If the buyer fails to remeasure, he cannot sell, dispose, or even consume (eat) the commodity until he does so. However, if he sells it without remeasuring, the sale is considered fasid (corrupt) because the quantity is unknown to the new buyer. The Hanafi school holds that this requirement applies only when selling by the same method (measure or weight); if the subsequent sale is by lump sum (juzafan), then remeasurement is not required.

Key Terms
مكيل (makil): Something that is sold by volume measure (e.g., grains).
موزون (mawzun): Something that is sold by weight (e.g., gold, silver, certain commodities).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling, if you buy wheat by measure, measure it yourself, and then sell it by measure to another person, what must you do?
A) You can use the same measurement.
B) You must remeasure it for the new buyer.
C) You do not need to measure at all.
D) You can only sell it by lump sum.

Key Takeaway
Every sale of measured/weighed goods requires a fresh measurement or weighing; the same measurement cannot be carried over from a previous transaction.
